  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part .- (1)\n'
  'The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the\n'
  'enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or\n'
  'writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, '
  'prohibition,\n'
  'quo warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the\n'
  'enforcement of any of the rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by\n'
  'clauses (1) and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to '
  'exercise\n'
  'within the local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers '
  'exercisable by\n'
  'the Supreme Court under clause (2).\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as\n'
  'otherwise provided for by this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '132A. [Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32.] .- Omitted by the Constitution (Forty-third\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978).\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc .- Parliament may, by law, determine to '
  'what\n'
  'extent any of the rights conferred by this Part shall, in their application '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the members of the Armed Forces; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of\n'
  'public order; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established\n'
  'by the State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) person employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication\n'
  'systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation\n'
  'referred to in clauses (a) to (c),\n'
  '\n'
  'be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their '
  'duties\n'
  'and the maintenance of discipline among them.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 6 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-2-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fiftieth Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'art. 33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 11-9-1984).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="20" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area .- Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing '
  'provisions\n'
  'of this Part, Parliament may by law indemnify any person in the service of '
  'the\n'
  'Union or of a State or any other person in respect of any act done by him '
  'in\n'
  'connection with the maintenance or restoration of order in any area within '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India where martial law was in force or validate any sentence\n'
  'passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or other act done under '
  'martial\n'
  'law in such area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not\n'
  'have, power to make laws-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of\n'
  'article 16, clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be\n'
  'provided for by law made by Parliament; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared\n'
  'to be offences under this Part,\n'
  '\n'
  'and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred\n'
  'to in sub-clause (ii);\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any law in force immediately before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters\n'
  'referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment '
  'for\n'
  'any act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to '
  'the\n'
  'terms thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made\n'
  'therein under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or\n'
  'amended by Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same\n'
  'meaning as in article 372.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART IV DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'
  '\n'
  '36\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" has the same meaning as in Part III.\n'
  '\n'
  '37\\. Application of the principles contained in this Part .- The\n'
  'provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, '
  'but the\n'
  'principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance '
  'of\n'
  'the country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles '
  'in\n'
  'making laws.\n'
  '\n'
  '38\\. State to secure a social order for the promotion of welfare of the\n'
  'people .- 1[(1)] The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the '
  'people by\n'
  'securing and protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which '
  'justice,\n'
  'social, economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the '
  'national life.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(2) The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities '
  'in\n'
  'income, and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and\n'
  'opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of '
  'people\n'
  'residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.]\n'
  '\n'
  '39\\. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State .- The\n'
  'State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) that the citizens, men and women equally, have the right to an\n'
  'adequate means of livelihood;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) that the ownership and control of the material resources of the\n'
  'community are so distributed as best to subserve the common good;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) that the operation of the economic system does not result in the\n'
  'concentration of wealth and means of production to the common\n'
  'detriment;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and\n'
  'the tender age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced\n'
  'by economic necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or\n'
  'strength;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 38 renumbered as cl. (1) by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 9 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 9, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="21" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="22" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## (Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(f) that children are given opportunities and facilities to develop\n'
  '☒\n'
  'in a healthy manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity and that\n'
  'childhood and youth are protected against exploitation and against moral\n'
  'and material abandonment.]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[39A. Equal justice and free legal aid .- The State shall secure that the\n'
  'operation of the legal system promotes justice, on a basis of equal '
  'opportunity,\n'
  'and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable legislation '
  'or schemes\n'
  'or in any other way, to ensure that opportunities for securing justice are '
  'not\n'
  'denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities.]\n',
  '\n'
  '"I, A.B., do swear in the name of God that I will faithfully execute the '
  'office\n'
  'solemnly affirm\n'
  '\n'
  'of President (or discharge the functions of the President) of India and '
  'will to the best\n'
  'of my ability preserve, protect and defend the Constitution and the law and '
  'that\n'
  'I will devote myself to the service and well-being of the people of '
  'India.".\n'
  '\n'
  '61\\. Procedure for impeachment of the President .- (1) When a\n'
  'President is to be impeached for violation of the Constitution, the charge '
  'shall\n'
  'be preferred by either House of Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No such charge shall be preferred unless-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the proposal to prefer such charge is contained in a resolution\n'
  "which has been moved after at least fourteen days' notice in writing\n"
  'signed by not less than one-fourth of the total number of members of the\n'
  'House has been given of their intention to move the resolution, and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) such resolution has been passed by a majority of not less than\n'
  'two-thirds of the total membership of the House.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) When a charge has been so preferred by either House of Parliament,\n'
  'the other House shall investigate the charge or cause the charge to be\n'
  'investigated and the President shall have the right to appear and to be\n'
  'represented at such investigation.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) If as a result of the investigation a resolution is passed by a '
  'majority\n'
  'of not less than two-thirds of the total membership of the House by which '
  'the\n'
  'charge was investigated or caused to be investigated, declaring that the '
  'charge\n'
  'preferred against the President has been sustained, such resolution shall '
  'have\n'
  'the effect of removing the President from his office as from the date on '
  'which\n'
  'the resolution is so passed.\n'
  '\n'
  '62\\. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of President\n'
  'and the term of office of person elected to fill casual vacancy .- (1) An\n'
  'election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of office '
  'of\n'
  'President shall be completed before the expiration of the term.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An election to fill a vacancy in the office of President occurring by\n'
  'reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise shall be held as '
  'soon\n'
  'as possible after, and in no case later than six months from, the date of\n'
  'occurrence of the vacancy; and the person elected to fill the vacancy '
  'shall,\n'
  'subject to the provisions of article 56, be entitled to hold office for the '
  'full term\n'
  'of five years from the date on which he enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '63\\. The Vice-President of India .- There shall be a Vice-President of '
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '64\\. The Vice-President to be ex officio Chairman of the Council of\n'
  'States .- The Vice-President shall be ex officio Chairman of the Council of '
  'the\n'
  'States and shall not hold any other office of profit:\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="30" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part V .- The Union)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that during any period when the Vice-President acts as\n'
  'President or discharges the functions of the President under article 65, he '
  'shall\n'
  'not perform the duties of the office of Chairman of the Council of States '
  'and\n'
  'shall not be entitled to any salary or allowance payable to the Chairman of '
  'the\n'
  'Council of States under article 97.\n'
  '\n'
  '65\\. The Vice-President to act as President or to discharge his\n'
  'functions during casual vacancies in the office, or during the absence,\n'
  'of President .- (1) In the event of the occurrence of any vacancy in the '
  'office\n'
  'of the President by reason of his death, resignation or removal, or '
  'otherwise,\n'
  'the Vice-President shall act as President until the date on which a new\n'
  'President elected in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter to fill '
  'such\n'
  'vacancy enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) When the President is unable to discharge his functions owing to\n'
  'absence, illness or any other cause, the Vice-President shall discharge '
  'his\n'
  'functions until the date on which the President resumes his duties.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The Vice-President shall, during, and in respect of, the period while\n'
  'he is so acting as, or discharging the functions of, President, have all '
  'the\n'
  'powers and immunities of the President and be entitled to such emoluments,\n'
  'allowances and privileges as may be determined by Parliament by law and,\n'
  'until provision in that behalf is so made, such emoluments, allowances and\n'
  'privileges as are specified in the Second Schedule.\n'
  '\n'
  '66\\. Election of Vice-President .- (1) The Vice-President shall be\n'
  'elected by the 1[members of an electoral college consisting of the members '
  'of\n'
  'both Houses of Parliament] in accordance with the system of proportional\n'
  'representation by means of the single transferable vote and the voting at '
  'such\n'
  'election shall be by secret ballot.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Vice-President shall not be a member of either House of\n'
  'Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State, and if a member '
  'of\n'
  'either House of Parliament or of a House of the Legislature of any State '
  'be\n'
  'elected Vice-President, he shall be deemed to have vacated his seat in '
  'that\n'
  'House on the date on which he enters upon his office as Vice-President.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person shall be eligible for election as Vice-President unless he-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) is a citizen of India;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) has completed the age of thirty-five years; and\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Eleventh Amendment) Act, 1961, s. 2, for '
  '"members of both\n'
  'Houses of Parliament assembled at a joint meeting" (w.e.f. 19-12-1961).\n'

  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'

  '\n'
  '(Part V .- The Union)\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) is qualified for election as a member of the Council of States.\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) A person shall not be eligible for election as Vice-President if he\n'
  'holds any office of profit under the Government of India or the Government '
  'of\n'
  'any State or under any local or other authority subject to the control of '
  'any of\n'
  'the said Governments.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- For the purposes of this article, a person shall not be\n'

  'or\n'

  '67\\. Term of office of Vice-President .- The Vice-President shall hold\n'
  'office for a term of five years from the date on which he enters upon his '
  'office:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) a Vice-President may, by writing under his hand addressed to the\n'
  'President, resign his office;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) a Vice-President may be removed from his office by a resolution\n'
  'of the Council of States passed by a majority of all the then members of\n'
  'the Council and agreed to by the House of the People; but no resolution\n'
  'for the purpose of this clause shall be moved unless at least fourteen\n'
  "days' notice has been given of the intention to move the resolution;\n"
  '\n'
  '(c) a Vice-President shall, notwithstanding the expiration of his term,\n'
  'continue to hold office until his successor enters upon his office.\n'
  '\n'
  '68\\. Time of holding election to fill vacancy in the office of Vice-\n'
  'President and the term of office of person elected to fill casual vacancy '
  '.-\n'
  '(1) An election to fill a vacancy caused by the expiration of the term of '
  'office\n'
  'of Vice-President shall be completed before the expiration of the term.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An election to fill a vacancy in the office of Vice-President\n'
  'occurring by reason of his death, resignation or removal, or otherwise '
  'shall be\n'
  'held as soon as possible after the occurrence of the vacancy, and the '
  'person\n'
  'elected to fill the vacancy shall, subject to the provisions of article 67, '
  'be\n'
  'entitled to hold office for the full term of five years from the date on '
  'which he\n'
  'enters upon his office.\n'

  '# PART XXII\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '# SHORT TITLE, COMMENCEMENT, "[AUTHORITATIVE TEXT IN HINDI] AND REPEALS\n'
  '\n'
  '393\\. Short title .- This Constitution may be called the Constitution of\n'
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '394\\. Commencement .- This article and articles 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 60, 324,\n'
  '366, 367, 379, 380, 388, 391, 392 and 393 shall come into force at once, '
  'and\n'
  'the remaining provisions of this Constitution shall come into force on the\n'
  'twenty-sixth day of January, 1950, which day is referred to in this '
  'Constitution\n'
  'as the commencement of this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[394A. Authoritative text in the Hindi language .- (1) The President\n'
  'shall cause to be published under his authority,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the translation of this Constitution in the Hindi language,\n'
  'signed by the members of the Constituent Assembly, with such\n'
  'modifications as may be necessary to bring it in conformity with the\n'
  'language, style and terminology adopted in the authoritative texts of\n'
  'Central Acts in the Hindi language, and incorporating therein all the\n'
  'amendments of this Constitution made before such publication; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the translation in the Hindi language of every amendment of\n'
  'this Constitution made in the English language.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The translation of this Constitution and of every amendment thereof\n'
  'published under clause (1) shall be construed to have the same meaning as '
  'the\n'
  'original thereof and if any difficulty arises in so construing any part of '
  'such\n'
  'translation, the President shall cause the same to be revised suitably.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) The translation of this Constitution and of every amendment thereof\n'
  'published under this article shall be deemed to be, for all purposes, the\n'
  'authoritative text thereof in the Hindi language.]\n'
  '\n'
  '395\\. Repeals .- The Indian Independence Act, 1947, and the\n'
  'Government of India Act, 1935, together with all enactments amending or\n'
  'supplementing the latter Act, but not including the Abolition of Privy '
  'Council\n'
  'Jurisdiction Act, 1949, are hereby repealed.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Fifty-eighth Amendment) Act, 1987, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 9-12-1987).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Art 394A, Ins. by s. 3, ibid. (w.e.f. 9-12-1987).\n'

  '\n'
  '## PART II CITIZENSHIP\n'
  '\n'
  '5\\. Citizenship at the commencement of the Constitution .- At the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution, every person who has his domicile in '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India and-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) who was born in the territory of India; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) either of whose parents was born in the territory of India; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) who has been ordinarily resident in the territory of India for\n'
  'not less than five years immediately preceding such commencement,\n'
  'shall be a citizen of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '6\\. Rights of citizenship of certain persons who have migrated to\n'
  'India from Pakistan .- Notwithstanding anything in article 5, a person who\n'
  'has migrated to the territory of India from the territory now included in\n'
  'Pakistan shall be deemed to be a citizen of India at the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution if-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) he or either of his parents or any of his grand-parents was born\n'
  'in India as defined in the Government of India Act, 1935 (as originally\n'
  'enacted); and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b)(i) in the case where such person has so migrated before the\n'
  'nineteenth day of July, 1948, he has been ordinarily resident in the\n'
  'territory of India since the date of his migration, or\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) in the case where such person has so migrated on or after the\n'
  'nineteenth day of July, 1948, he has been registered as a citizen of India\n'
  'by an officer appointed in that behalf by the Government of the\n'
  'Dominion of India on an application made by him therefor to such\n'
  'officer before the commencement of this Constitution in the form and\n'
  'manner prescribed by that Government:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that no person shall be so registered unless he has been resident\n'
  'in the territory of India for at least six months immediately preceding the '
  'date\n'
  'of his application.\n'
  '\n'
  '7\\. Rights of citizenship of certain migrants to Pakistan .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in articles 5 and 6, a person who has after the '
  'first\n'
  'day of March, 1947, migrated from the territory of India to the territory '
  'now\n'
  'included in Pakistan shall not be deemed to be a citizen of India:\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="4" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="5" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part II .- Citizenship)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that nothing in this article shall apply to a person who, after\n'
  'having so migrated to the territory now included in Pakistan, has returned '
  'to the\n'
  'territory of India under a permit for resettlement or permanent return '
  'issued by\n'
  'or under the authority of any law and every such person shall for the '
  'purposes\n'
  'of clause (b) of article 6 be deemed to have migrated to the territory of '
  'India\n'
  'after the nineteenth day of July, 1948.\n'
  '\n'
  '8\\. Rights of citizenship of certain persons of Indian origin residing\n'
  'outside India .- Notwithstanding anything in article 5, any person who or\n'
  'either of whose parents or any of whose grand-parents was born in India as\n'
  'defined in the Government of India Act, 1935 (as originally enacted), and '
  'who\n'
  'is ordinarily residing in any country outside India as so defined shall be '
  'deemed\n'
  'to be a citizen of India if he has been registered as a citizen of India by '
  'the\n'
  'diplomatic or consular representative of India in the country where he is '
  'for the\n'
  'time being residing on an application made by him therefor to such '
  'diplomatic\n'
  'or consular representative, whether before or after the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution, in the form and manner prescribed by the Government of the\n'
  'Dominion of India or the Government of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '9\\. Persons voluntarily acquiring citizenship of a foreign State not to\n'
  'be citizens .- No person shall be a citizen of India by virtue of article '
  '5, or be\n'
  'deemed to be a citizen of India by virtue of article 6 or article 8, if he '
  'has\n'
  'voluntarily acquired the citizenship of any foreign State.\n'
  '\n'
  '10\\. Continuance of the rights of citizenship .- Every person who is or\n'
  'is deemed to be a citizen of India under any of the foregoing provisions of '
  'this\n'
  'Part shall, subject to the provisions of any law that may be made by '
  'Parliament,\n'
  'continue to be such citizen.\n'
  '\n'
  '11\\. Parliament to regulate the right of citizenship by law .- Nothing\n'
  'in the foregoing provisions of this Part shall derogate from the power of\n'
  'Parliament to make any provision with respect to the acquisition and\n'
  'termination of citizenship and all other matters relating to citizenship.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART III FUNDAMENTAL RIGHTS\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### General\n'
  '\n'
  '12\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" includes the Government and Parliament of India and the Government\n'
  'and the Legislature of each of the States and all local or other '
  'authorities within\n'
  'the territory of India or under the control of the Government of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '13\\. Laws inconsistent with or in derogation of the fundamental\n'
  'rights .- (1) All laws in force in the territory of India immediately '
  'before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution, in so far as they are inconsistent with '
  'the\n'
  'provisions of this Part, shall, to the extent of such inconsistency, be '
  'void.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The State shall not make any law which takes away or abridges the\n'
  'rights conferred by this Part and any law made in contravention of this '
  'clause\n'
  'shall, to the extent of the contravention, be void.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) In this article, unless the context otherwise requires,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) "law" includes any Ordinance, order, bye-law, rule, regulation,\n'
  'notification, custom or usage having in the territory of India the force '
  'of\n'
  'law;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) "laws in force" includes laws passed or made by a Legislature\n'
  'or other competent authority in the territory of India before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution and not previously repealed,\n'
  'notwithstanding that any such law or any part thereof may not be then in\n'
  'operation either at all or in particular areas.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(4) Nothing in this article shall apply to any amendment of this\n'
  'Constitution made under article 368.]\n'
  '\n'
  'Right to Equality\n'
  '\n'
  '14\\. Equality before law .- The State shall not deny to any person\n'
  'equality before the law or the equal protection of the laws within the '
  'territory of\n'
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '15\\. Prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, race, caste,\n'
  'sex or place of birth .- (1) The State shall not discriminate against any '
  'citizen\n'
  'on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, place of birth or any of '
  'them.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, place '
  'of\n'
  'birth or any of them, be subject to any disability, liability, restriction '
  'or\n'
  'condition with regard to-\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Twenty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1971, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="6" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="7" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) access to shops, public restaurants, hotels and places of public\n'
  'entertainment; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the use of wells, tanks, bathing ghats, roads and places of\n'
  'public resort maintained wholly or partly out of State funds or dedicated\n'
  'to the use of the general public.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any\n'
  'special provision for women and children.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(4) Nothing in this article or in clause (2) of article 29 shall prevent '
  'the\n'
  'State from making any special provision for the advancement of any '
  'socially\n'
  'and educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled Castes '
  'and\n'
  'the Scheduled Tribes.]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(5) Nothing in this article or in sub-clause (g) of clause (1) of article '
  '19\n',
  '\n'
  '7\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 5 '
  '(w.e.f. 03-01-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="19" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right to Constitutional Remedies\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Remedies for enforcement of rights conferred by this Part .- (1)\n'
  'The right to move the Supreme Court by appropriate proceedings for the\n'
  'enforcement of the rights conferred by this Part is guaranteed.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The Supreme Court shall have power to issue directions or orders or\n'
  'writs, including writs in the nature of habeas corpus, mandamus, '
  'prohibition,\n'
  'quo warranto and certiorari, whichever may be appropriate, for the\n'
  'enforcement of any of the rights conferred by this Part.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Without prejudice to the powers conferred on the Supreme Court by\n'
  'clauses (1) and (2), Parliament may by law empower any other court to '
  'exercise\n'
  'within the local limits of its jurisdiction all or any of the powers '
  'exercisable by\n'
  'the Supreme Court under clause (2).\n'
  '\n'
  '(4) The right guaranteed by this article shall not be suspended except as\n'
  'otherwise provided for by this Constitution.\n'
  '\n'
  '132A. [Constitutional validity of State laws not to be considered in\n'
  'proceedings under article 32.] .- Omitted by the Constitution (Forty-third\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1977, s. 3 (w.e.f. 13-4-1978).\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Power of Parliament to modify the rights conferred by this Part\n'
  'in their application to Forces, etc .- Parliament may, by law, determine to '
  'what\n'
  'extent any of the rights conferred by this Part shall, in their application '
  'to,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the members of the Armed Forces; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the members of the Forces charged with the maintenance of\n'
  'public order; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) persons employed in any bureau or other organisation established\n'
  'by the State for purposes of intelligence or counter intelligence; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) person employed in, or in connection with, the telecommunication\n'
  'systems set up for the purposes of any Force, bureau or organisation\n'
  'referred to in clauses (a) to (c),\n'
  '\n'
  'be restricted or abrogated so as to ensure the proper discharge of their '
  'duties\n'
  'and the maintenance of discipline among them.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 6 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-2-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Fiftieth Amendment) Act, 1984, s. 2, for '
  'art. 33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 11-9-1984).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="20" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '34\\. Restriction on rights conferred by this Part while martial law is\n'
  'in force in any area .- Notwithstanding anything in the foregoing '
  'provisions\n'
  'of this Part, Parliament may by law indemnify any person in the service of '
  'the\n'
  'Union or of a State or any other person in respect of any act done by him '
  'in\n'
  'connection with the maintenance or restoration of order in any area within '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India where martial law was in force or validate any sentence\n'
  'passed, punishment inflicted, forfeiture ordered or other act done under '
  'martial\n'
  'law in such area.\n'
  '\n'
  '35\\. Legislation to give effect to the provisions of this Part .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) Parliament shall have, and the Legislature of a State shall not\n'
  'have, power to make laws-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) with respect to any of the matters which under clause (3) of\n'
  'article 16, clause (3) of article 32, article 33 and article 34 may be\n'
  'provided for by law made by Parliament; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) for prescribing punishment for those acts which are declared\n'
  'to be offences under this Part,\n'
  '\n'
  'and Parliament shall, as soon as may be after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, make laws for prescribing punishment for the acts referred\n'
  'to in sub-clause (ii);\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any law in force immediately before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution in the territory of India with respect to any of the matters\n'
  'referred to in sub-clause (i) of clause (a) or providing for punishment '
  'for\n'
  'any act referred to in sub-clause (ii) of that clause shall, subject to '
  'the\n'
  'terms thereof and to any adaptations and modifications that may be made\n'
  'therein under article 372, continue in force until altered or repealed or\n'
  'amended by Parliament.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- In this article, the expression "law in force" has the same\n'
  'meaning as in article 372.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART IV DIRECTIVE PRINCIPLES OF STATE POLICY\n'
  '\n'
  '36\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" has the same meaning as in Part III.\n'
  '\n'
  '37\\. Application of the principles contained in this Part .- The\n'
  'provisions contained in this Part shall not be enforceable by any court, '
  'but the\n'
  'principles therein laid down are nevertheless fundamental in the governance '
  'of\n'
  'the country and it shall be the duty of the State to apply these principles '
  'in\n'
  'making laws.\n'
  '\n'
  '38\\. State to secure a social order for the promotion of welfare of the\n'
  'people .- 1[(1)] The State shall strive to promote the welfare of the '
  'people by\n'
  'securing and protecting as effectively as it may a social order in which '
  'justice,\n'
  'social, economic and political, shall inform all the institutions of the '
  'national life.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(2) The State shall, in particular, strive to minimise the inequalities '
  'in\n'
  'income, and endeavour to eliminate inequalities in status, facilities and\n'
  'opportunities, not only amongst individuals but also amongst groups of '
  'people\n'
  'residing in different areas or engaged in different vocations.]\n'
  '\n'
  '39\\. Certain principles of policy to be followed by the State .- The\n'
  'State shall, in particular, direct its policy towards securing-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) that the citizens, men and women equally, have the right to an\n'
  'adequate means of livelihood;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) that the ownership and control of the material resources of the\n'
  'community are so distributed as best to subserve the common good;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) that the operation of the economic system does not result in the\n'
  'concentration of wealth and means of production to the common\n'
  'detriment;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) that there is equal pay for equal work for both men and women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) that the health and strength of workers, men and women, and\n'
  'the tender age of children are not abused and that citizens are not forced\n'
  'by economic necessity to enter avocations unsuited to their age or\n'
  'strength;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 38 renumbered as cl. (1) by the Constitution (Forty-fourth '
  'Amendment) Act,\n'
  '1978, s. 9 (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 9, ibid. (w.e.f. 20-6-1979).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="21" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="22" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## (Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(f) that children are given opportunities and facilities to develop\n'
  '☒\n'
  'in a healthy manner and in conditions of freedom and dignity and that\n'
  'childhood and youth are protected against exploitation and against moral\n'
  'and material abandonment.]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[39A. Equal justice and free legal aid .- The State shall secure that the\n'
  'operation of the legal system promotes justice, on a basis of equal '
  'opportunity,\n'
  'and shall, in particular, provide free legal aid, by suitable legislation '
  'or schemes\n'
  'or in any other way, to ensure that opportunities for securing justice are '
  'not\n'
  'denied to any citizen by reason of economic or other disabilities.]\n'],
 ['\n'
  '40\\. Organisation of village panchayats .- The State shall take steps to\n'
  'organise village panchayats and endow them with such powers and authority '
  'as\n'
  'may be necessary to enable them to function as units of self-government.\n'
  '\n'
  '41\\. Right to work, to education and to public assistance in certain\n'
  'cases .- The State shall, within the limits of its economic capacity and\n'
  'development, make effective provision for securing the right to work, to\n'
  'education and to public assistance in cases of unemployment, old age, '
  'sickness\n'
  'and disablement, and in other cases of undeserved want.\n'
  '\n'
  '42\\. Provision for just and humane conditions of work and maternity\n'
  'relief .- The State shall make provision for securing just and humane\n'
  'conditions of work and for maternity relief.\n'
  '\n'
  '43\\. Living wage, etc., for workers .- The State shall endeavour to\n'
  'secure, by suitable legislation or economic organisation or in any other '
  'way, to\n'
  'all workers, agricultural, industrial or otherwise, work, a living wage,\n'
  'conditions of work ensuring a decent standard of life and full enjoyment '
  'of\n'
  'leisure and social and cultural opportunities and, in particular, the State '
  'shall\n'
  'endeavour to promote cottage industries on an individual or co-operative '
  'basis\n'
  'in rural areas.\n'
  '\n'
  '3[43A. Participation of workers in management of industries .- The\n'
  'State shall take steps, by suitable legislation or in any other way, to '
  'secure the\n'
  'participation of workers in the management of undertakings, establishments '
  'or\n'
  'other organisations engaged in any industry.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 7, '

  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[43B. Promotion of co-operative societies .- The State shall endeavour\n'
  'to promote voluntary formation, autonomous functioning, democratic control\n'
  'and professional management of co-operative societies.]\n'
  '\n'
  '44\\. Uniform civil code for the citizens .- The State shall endeavour to\n'
  'secure for the citizens a uniform civil code throughout the territory of '
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[45. Provision for early childhood care and education to children\n'
  'below the age of six years .- The State shall endeavour to provide early\n'
  'childhood care and education for all children until they complete the age '
  'of six\n'
  'years.]\n'
  '\n'
  '46\\. Promotion of educational and economic interests of Scheduled\n'
  'Castes, Scheduled Tribes and other weaker sections .- The State shall\n'
  'promote with special care the educational and economic interests of the '
  'weaker\n'
  'sections of the people, and, in particular, of the Scheduled Castes and '
  'the\n'
  'Scheduled Tribes, and shall protect them from social injustice and all '
  'forms of\n'
  'exploitation.\n'
  '\n'
  '47\\. Duty of the State to raise the level of nutrition and the standard\n'
  'of living and to improve public health .- The State shall regard the '
  'raising of\n'
  'the level of nutrition and the standard of living of its people and the\n'
  'improvement of public health as among its primary duties and, in '
  'particular, the\n'
  'State shall endeavour to bring about prohibition of the consumption except '
  'for\n'
  'medicinal purposes of intoxicating drinks and of drugs which are injurious '
  'to\n'
  'health.\n'
  '\n'
  '48\\. Organisation of agriculture and animal husbandry .- The State\n'
  'shall endeavour to organise agriculture and animal husbandry on modern and\n'
  'scientific lines and shall, in particular, take steps for preserving and '
  'improving\n'
  'the breeds, and prohibiting the slaughter, of cows and calves and other '
  'milch\n'
  'and draught cattle.\n'
  '\n'
  '3[48A. Protection and improvement of environment and\n'
  'safeguarding of forests and wild life .- The State shall endeavour to '
  'protect\n'
  'and improve the environment and to safeguard the forests and wild life of '
  'the\n'
  'country.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Ninety-seventh Amendment) Act, 2011, s. 3 '
  '(w.e.f. 15-2-2012).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Eighty-sixth Amendment) Act, 2002, s. 3, '

  '(w.e.f. 1-4-2010).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 10 '

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '(Part IV .- Directive Principles of State Policy)\n'
  '\n'
  '49\\. Protection of monuments and places and objects of national\n'
  'importance .- It shall be the obligation of the State to protect every '
  'monument\n'
  'or place or object of artistic or historic interest, 1[declared by or under '
  'law\n'
  'made by Parliament] to be of national importance, from spoliation,\n'
  'disfigurement, destruction, removal, disposal or export, as the case may '
  'be.\n'
  '\n'
  '50\\. Separation of judiciary from executive .- The State shall take steps\n'
  'to separate the judiciary from the executive in the public services of the '
  'State.\n'
  '\n'
  '51\\. Promotion of international peace and security .- The State shall\n'
  'endeavour to-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) promote international peace and security;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) maintain just and honourable relations between nations;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) foster respect for international law and treaty obligations in the\n'
  'dealings of organised peoples with one another; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) encourage settlement of international disputes by arbitration.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Seventh Amendment) Act, 1956, s. 27, for '
  '"declared by\n'
  'Parliament by law" (w.e.f. 1-11-1956).\n'

  '## "[PART IVA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## FUNDAMENTAL DUTIES\n'
  '\n'
  '51A. Fundamental duties .- It shall be the duty of every citizen of\n'
  'India-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to abide by the Constitution and respect its ideals and\n'
  'institutions, the National Flag and the National Anthem;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to cherish and follow the noble ideals which inspired our\n'
  'national struggle for freedom;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to uphold and protect the sovereignty, unity and integrity of\n'
  'India;\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to defend the country and render national service when called\n'
  'upon to do so;\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) to promote harmony and the spirit of common brotherhood\n'
  'amongst all the people of India transcending religious, linguistic and\n'
  'regional or sectional diversities; to renounce practices derogatory to the\n'
  'dignity of women;\n'
  '\n'
  '(f) to value and preserve the rich heritage of our composite\n'
  'culture;\n'
  '\n'
  '(g) to protect and improve the natural environment including\n'
  'forests, lakes, rivers and wild life, and to have compassion for living\n'
  'creatures;\n'
  '\n'
  '(h) to develop the scientific temper, humanism and the spirit of\n'
  'inquiry and reform;\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) to safeguard public property and to abjure violence;\n'
  '\n'
  '(j) to strive towards excellence in all spheres of individual and\n'
  'collective activity so that the nation constantly rises to higher levels '
  'of\n'
  'endeavour and achievement; ]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(k) who is a parent or guardian to provide opportunities for\n'
  'education to his child or, as the case may be, ward between the age of\n'
  'six and fourteen years.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 11 '
  '(w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Eighty-sixth Amendment) Act, 2002, s. 4 '
  '(w.e.f. 1-4-2010).\n'

  '\n'
  '# PART XXI\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '# 1[TEMPORARY, TRANSITIONAL AND SPECIAL PROVISIONS]\n'
  '\n'
  '369\\. Temporary power to Parliament to make laws with respect to\n'
  'certain matters in the State List as if they were matters in the '
  'Concurrent\n'
  'List .- Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, Parliament shall, '
  'during\n'
  'a period of five years from the commencement of this Constitution, have '
  'power\n'
  'to make laws with respect to the following matters as if they were '
  'enumerated\n'
  'in the Concurrent List, namely :-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) trade and commerce within a State in, and the production, supply\n'
  'and distribution of, cotton and woollen textiles, raw cotton (including\n'
  'ginned cotton and unginned cotton or kapas), cotton seed, paper\n'
  '(including newsprint), food-stuffs (including edible oilseeds and oil),\n'
  'cattle fodder (including oil-cakes and other concentrates), coal\n'
  '(including coke and derivatives of coal), iron, steel and mica;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) offences against laws with respect to any of the matters mentioned\n'
  'in clause (a), jurisdiction and powers of all courts except the Supreme\n'
  'Court with respect to any of those matters, and fees in respect of any of\n'
  'those matters but not including fees taken in any court,\n'
  '\n'
  'but any law made by Parliament, which Parliament would not but for the\n'
  'provisions of this article have been competent to make, shall, to the '
  'extent of the\n'
  'incompetency, cease to have effect on the expiration of the said period, '
  'except as\n'
  'respects things done or omitted to be done before the expiration thereof.\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Thirteenth Amendment) Act, 1962, s. 2, for '
  '"TEMPORARY\n'
  'AND TRANSITIONAL PROVISIONS" (w.e.f. 1-12-1963).\n'

  'of Jammu and Kashmir;\n'
  '\n'

  'limited to-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) those matters in the Union List and the Concurrent List\n'
  'which, in consultation with the Government of the State, are declared\n'
  'by the President to correspond to matters specified in the Instrument\n'
  'of Accession governing the accession of the State to the Dominion of\n'
  'India as the matters with respect to which the Dominion Legislature\n'
  'may make laws for that State; and\n'
  '\n'

  'with clause (1) of\n'

  'recommendation of\n'
  'Parliament, is pleased to declare that, as from the 6th August, 2019 all '
  'clauses of said\n'
  'article 370 shall cease to be operative except the following which shall '
  'read as under,\n'
  'namely :-\n'
  '\n'

  'without any modifications or exceptions, shall apply to the State of Jammu '

  'article 363 or\n'
  'otherwise.".\n'

  '(Part XVI .- Special Provisions Relating to Certain Classes)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[Provided that nothing in this article shall prevent in making of any\n'
  'provision in favour of the members of the Scheduled Castes and the '
  'Scheduled\n'
  'Tribes for relaxation in qualifying marks in any examination or lowering '
  'the\n'
  'standards of evaluation, for reservation in matters or promotion to any '
  'class or\n'
  'classes of services or posts in connection with the affairs of the Union or '
  'of a State.]\n'
  '\n'
  '336\\. Special provision for Anglo-Indian community in certain\n'
  'services .- (1) During the first two years after the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution, appointments of members of the Anglo-Indian community to '
  'posts\n'
  'in the railway, customs, postal and telegraph services of the Union shall '
  'be made\n'
  'on the same basis as immediately before the fifteenth day of August, 1947.\n'
  '\n'
  'During every succeeding period of two years, the number of posts\n'
  'reserved for the members of the said community in the said services shall, '
  'as\n'
  'nearly as possible, be less by ten per cent. than the numbers so reserved '
  'during\n'
  'the immediately preceding period of two years:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution all such reservations shall cease.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall bar the appointment of members of the\n'
  'Anglo-Indian community to posts other than, or in addition to, those '
  'reserved\n'
  'for the community under that clause if such members are found qualified '
  'for\n'
  'appointment on merit as compared with the members of other communities.\n'
  '\n'
  '337\\. Special provision with respect to educational grants for the\n'
  'benefit of Anglo-Indian community .- During the first three financial '
  'years\n'
  'after the commencement of this Constitution, the same grants, if any, shall '
  'be\n'
  'made by the Union and by each State 2 *** for the benefit of the '
  'Anglo-Indian\n'
  'community in respect of education as were made in the financial year '
  'ending\n'
  'on the thirty-first day of March, 1948.\n'
  '\n'
  'During every succeeding period of three years the grants may be less by\n'
  'ten per cent. than those for the immediately preceding period of three '
  'years:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that at the end of ten years from the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution such grants, to the extent to which they are a special '
  'concession to\n'
  'the Anglo-Indian community, shall cease:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided further that no educational institution shall be entitled to\n'
  'receive any grant under this article unless at least forty per cent. of the '
  'annual\n'
  'admissions therein are made available to members of communities other than\n'
  'the Anglo-Indian community.\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'
  'Provided that nothing in this sub-clause shall authorise the detention\n'
  'of any person beyond the maximum period prescribed by any law made\n'

  '\n'

  '\n'

  'any law providing for preventive detention, the authority making the order\n'
  'shall, as soon as may be, communicate to such person the grounds on which '
  'the\n'
  'order has been made and shall afford him the earliest opportunity of making '
  'a\n'
  'representation against the order.\n'
  '\n'

  'order as is referred to in that clause to disclose facts which such '
  'authority\n'
  'considers to be against the public interest to disclose.\n'
  '\n'

  '\n'

  'sub-clause (a) of clause (4);\n'

  'detention; and\n'
  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Right against Exploitation\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Prohibition of traffic in human beings and forced labour .- (1)\n'
  'Traffic in human beings and begar and other similar forms of forced labour '
  'are\n'
  'prohibited and any contravention of this provision shall be an offence\n'
  'punishable in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from imposing\n'
  'compulsory service for public purposes, and in imposing such service the '
  'State\n'
  'shall not make any discrimination on grounds only of religion, race, caste '
  'or\n'
  'class or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Prohibition of employment of children in factories, etc .- No child\n'
  'below the age of fourteen years shall be employed to work in any factory '
  'or\n'
  'mine or engaged in any other hazardous employment.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '##### Right to Freedom of Religion\n'
  '\n'
  '25\\. Freedom of conscience and free profession, practice and\n'
  'propagation of religion .- (1) Subject to public order, morality and health '
  'and\n'
  'to the other provisions of this Part, all persons are equally entitled to '
  'freedom\n'
  'of conscience and the right freely to profess, practice and propagate '
  'religion.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in this article shall affect the operation of any existing law '
  'or\n'
  'prevent the State from making any law-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) regulating or restricting any economic, financial, political or\n'
  'other secular activity which may be associated with religious practice;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) providing for social welfare and reform or the throwing open\n'
  'of Hindu religious institutions of a public character to all classes and\n'
  'sections of Hindus.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation I .- The wearing and carrying of kirpans shall be deemed to\n'
  'be included in the profession of the Sikh religion.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation II .- In sub-clause (b) of clause (2), the reference to Hindus\n'
  'shall be construed as including a reference to persons professing the Sikh, '
  'Jaina\n'
  'or Buddhist religion, and the reference to Hindu religious institutions '
  'shall be\n'
  'construed accordingly.\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Freedom to manage religious affairs .- Subject to public order,\n'
  'morality and health, every religious denomination or any section thereof '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) to establish and maintain institutions for religious and charitable\n'
  'purposes;\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="15" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) to manage its own affairs in matters of religion;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) to own and acquire movable and immovable property; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) to administer such property in accordance with law.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Freedom as to payment of taxes for promotion of any particular\n'
  'religion .- No person shall be compelled to pay any taxes, the proceeds of\n'
  'which are specifically appropriated in payment of expenses for the '
  'promotion\n'
  'or maintenance of any particular religion or religious denomination.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Freedom as to attendance at religious instruction or religious\n'
  'worship in certain educational institutions .- (1) No religious '
  'instruction\n'
  'shall be provided in any educational institution wholly maintained out of '
  'State\n'
  'funds.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) Nothing in clause (1) shall apply to an educational institution which\n'
  'is administered by the State but has been established under any endowment '
  'or\n'
  'trust which requires that religious instruction shall be imparted in such\n'
  'institution.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) No person attending any educational institution recognised by the\n'
  'State or receiving aid out of State funds shall be required to take part in '
  'any\n'
  'religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend '
  'any\n'
  'religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any '
  'premises\n'
  'attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his '
  'guardian\n'
  'has given his consent thereto.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '#### Cultural and Educational Rights\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Protection of interests of minorities .- (1) Any section of the\n'
  'citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a '
  'distinct\n'
  'language, script or culture of its own shall have the right to conserve the '
  'same.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution\n'
  'maintained by the State or receiving aid out of State funds on grounds only '
  'of\n'
  'religion, race, caste, language or any of them.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Right of minorities to establish and administer educational\n'
  'institutions .- (1) All minorities, whether based on religion or language, '
  'shall\n'
  'have the right to establish and administer educational institutions of '
  'their\n'
  'choice.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="16" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(1A) In making any law providing for the compulsory acquisition of\n'
  'any property of an educational institution established and administered by '
  'a\n'
  'minority, referred to in clause (1), the State shall ensure that the amount '
  'fixed\n'
  'by or determined under such law for the acquisition of such property is '
  'such as\n'
  'would not restrict or abrogate the right guaranteed under that clause.]\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The State shall not, in granting aid to educational institutions,\n'
  'discriminate against any educational institution on the ground that it is '
  'under\n'
  'the management of a minority, whether based on religion or language.\n'

  '## PREFACE\n'
  '\n'
  'This is the sixth pocket size edition of the Constitution of\n'
  'India in the diglot form. In this edition, the text of the\n'
  'Constitution of India has been brought up-to-date by\n'
  'incorporating therein all the amendments up to the Constitution\n'
  '(One Hundred and Sixth Amendment) Act, 2023. The foot notes\n'
  'below the text indicate the Constitution Amendment Acts by\n'
  'which such amendments have been made.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (One Hundredth Amendment) Act, 2015\n'
  'containing details of acquired and transferred territories\n'
  'between the Governments of India and Bangladesh has been\n'
  'provided in Appendix I.\n'
  '\n'
  'The Constitution (Application to Jammu and Kashmir)\n'
  'Order, 2019 and the declaration under article 370(3) of the\n'
  'Constitution have been provided respectively in Appendix II and\n'
  'Appendix III for reference.\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'

  'Sikkim to be associated with the Union .- Omitted.]\n'

  'Formation of new States and alteration of areas, boundaries or\n'
  'names of existing States.\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\.\n'
  'Laws made under articles 2 and 3 to provide for the amendment of\n'
  'the First and the Fourth Schedules and supplemental, incidental\n'
  'and consequential matters.\n'

  '\n'
  '## PART II CITIZENSHIP\n'
  '\n'
  '5\\. Citizenship at the commencement of the Constitution .- At the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution, every person who has his domicile in '
  'the\n'
  'territory of India and-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) who was born in the territory of India; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) either of whose parents was born in the territory of India; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) who has been ordinarily resident in the territory of India for\n'
  'not less than five years immediately preceding such commencement,\n'
  'shall be a citizen of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '6\\. Rights of citizenship of certain persons who have migrated to\n'
  'India from Pakistan .- Notwithstanding anything in article 5, a person who\n'
  'has migrated to the territory of India from the territory now included in\n'
  'Pakistan shall be deemed to be a citizen of India at the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution if-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) he or either of his parents or any of his grand-parents was born\n'
  'in India as defined in the Government of India Act, 1935 (as originally\n'
  'enacted); and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b)(i) in the case where such person has so migrated before the\n'
  'nineteenth day of July, 1948, he has been ordinarily resident in the\n'
  'territory of India since the date of his migration, or\n'
  '\n'
  '(ii) in the case where such person has so migrated on or after the\n'
  'nineteenth day of July, 1948, he has been registered as a citizen of India\n'
  'by an officer appointed in that behalf by the Government of the\n'
  'Dominion of India on an application made by him therefor to such\n'
  'officer before the commencement of this Constitution in the form and\n'
  'manner prescribed by that Government:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that no person shall be so registered unless he has been resident\n'
  'in the territory of India for at least six months immediately preceding the '
  'date\n'
  'of his application.\n'
  '\n'
  '7\\. Rights of citizenship of certain migrants to Pakistan .-\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in articles 5 and 6, a person who has after the '
  'first\n'
  'day of March, 1947, migrated from the territory of India to the territory '
  'now\n'
  'included in Pakistan shall not be deemed to be a citizen of India:\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="4" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="5" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part II .- Citizenship)\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that nothing in this article shall apply to a person who, after\n'
  'having so migrated to the territory now included in Pakistan, has returned '
  'to the\n'
  'territory of India under a permit for resettlement or permanent return '
  'issued by\n'
  'or under the authority of any law and every such person shall for the '
  'purposes\n'
  'of clause (b) of article 6 be deemed to have migrated to the territory of '
  'India\n'
  'after the nineteenth day of July, 1948.\n'
  '\n'
  '8\\. Rights of citizenship of certain persons of Indian origin residing\n'
  'outside India .- Notwithstanding anything in article 5, any person who or\n'
  'either of whose parents or any of whose grand-parents was born in India as\n'
  'defined in the Government of India Act, 1935 (as originally enacted), and '
  'who\n'
  'is ordinarily residing in any country outside India as so defined shall be '
  'deemed\n'
  'to be a citizen of India if he has been registered as a citizen of India by '
  'the\n'
  'diplomatic or consular representative of India in the country where he is '
  'for the\n'
  'time being residing on an application made by him therefor to such '
  'diplomatic\n'
  'or consular representative, whether before or after the commencement of '
  'this\n'
  'Constitution, in the form and manner prescribed by the Government of the\n'
  'Dominion of India or the Government of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '9\\. Persons voluntarily acquiring citizenship of a foreign State not to\n'
  'be citizens .- No person shall be a citizen of India by virtue of article '
  '5, or be\n'
  'deemed to be a citizen of India by virtue of article 6 or article 8, if he '
  'has\n'
  'voluntarily acquired the citizenship of any foreign State.\n'
  '\n'
  '10\\. Continuance of the rights of citizenship .- Every person who is or\n'
  'is deemed to be a citizen of India under any of the foregoing provisions of '
  'this\n'
  'Part shall, subject to the provisions of any law that may be made by '
  'Parliament,\n'
  'continue to be such citizen.\n'
  '\n'
  '11\\. Parliament to regulate the right of citizenship by law .- Nothing\n'
  'in the foregoing provisions of this Part shall derogate from the power of\n'
  'Parliament to make any provision with respect to the acquisition and\n'
  'termination of citizenship and all other matters relating to citizenship.\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## PART III FUNDAMENTAL RIGHTS\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### General\n'
  '\n'
  '12\\. Definition .- In this Part, unless the context otherwise requires, '
  '"the\n'
  'State" includes the Government and Parliament of India and the Government\n'
  'and the Legislature of each of the States and all local or other '
  'authorities within\n'
  'the territory of India or under the control of the Government of India.\n'
  '\n'
  '13\\. Laws inconsistent with or in derogation of the fundamental\n'
  'rights .- (1) All laws in force in the territory of India immediately '
  'before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution, in so far as they are inconsistent with '
  'the\n'
  'provisions of this Part, shall, to the extent of such inconsistency, be '
  'void.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) The State shall not make any law which takes away or abridges the\n'
  'rights conferred by this Part and any law made in contravention of this '
  'clause\n'
  'shall, to the extent of the contravention, be void.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) In this article, unless the context otherwise requires,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) "law" includes any Ordinance, order, bye-law, rule, regulation,\n'
  'notification, custom or usage having in the territory of India the force '
  'of\n'
  'law;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) "laws in force" includes laws passed or made by a Legislature\n'
  'or other competent authority in the territory of India before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution and not previously repealed,\n'
  'notwithstanding that any such law or any part thereof may not be then in\n'
  'operation either at all or in particular areas.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(4) Nothing in this article shall apply to any amendment of this\n'
  'Constitution made under article 368.]\n'
  '\n'
  'Right to Equality\n'
  '\n'
  '14\\. Equality before law .- The State shall not deny to any person\n'
  'equality before the law or the equal protection of the laws within the '
  'territory of\n'
  'India.\n'
  '\n'
  '15\\. Prohibition of discrimination on grounds of religion, race, caste,\n'
  'sex or place of birth .- (1) The State shall not discriminate against any '
  'citizen\n'
  'on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, place of birth or any of '
  'them.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) No citizen shall, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, sex, place '
  'of\n'
  'birth or any of them, be subject to any disability, liability, restriction '
  'or\n'
  'condition with regard to-\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Ins. by the Constitution (Twenty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1971, s. 2 '
  '(w.e.f. 5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="6" -->\n'
  '<!-- PageBreak -->\n'
  '\n'
  '<!-- PageNumber="7" -->\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA\n'
  '\n'
  '\n'
  '### (Part III .- Fundamental Rights)\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) access to shops, public restaurants, hotels and places of public\n'
  'entertainment; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the use of wells, tanks, bathing ghats, roads and places of\n'
  'public resort maintained wholly or partly out of State funds or dedicated\n'
  'to the use of the general public.\n'
  '\n'
  '(3) Nothing in this article shall prevent the State from making any\n'
  'special provision for women and children.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[(4) Nothing in this article or in clause (2) of article 29 shall prevent '
  'the\n'
  'State from making any special provision for the advancement of any '
  'socially\n'
  'and educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled Castes '
  'and\n'
  'the Scheduled Tribes.]\n'
  '\n'
  '2[(5) Nothing in this article or in sub-clause (g) of clause (1) of article '
  '19\n',
  '57 (w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'

  '## THE CONSTITUTION OF INDIA (Seventh Schedule)\n'
  '\n'
  '21\\. Commercial and industrial monopolies, combines and trusts.\n'
  '\n'
  '22\\. Trade unions; industrial and labour disputes.\n'
  '\n'
  '23\\. Social security and social insurance; employment and unemployment.\n'
  '\n'
  '24\\. Welfare of labour including conditions of work, provident funds,\n'
  "employers' liability, workmen's compensation, invalidity and old age "
  'pensions\n'
  'and maternity benefits.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[25. Education, including technical education, medical education and\n'
  'universities, subject to the provisions of entries 63, 64, 65 and 66 of '
  'List I;\n'
  'vocational and technical training of labour.]\n'
  '\n'
  '26\\. Legal, medical and other professions.\n'
  '\n'
  '27\\. Relief and rehabilitation of persons displaced from their original '
  'place\n'
  'of residence by reason of the setting up of the Dominions of India and '
  'Pakistan.\n'
  '\n'
  '28\\. Charities and charitable institutions, charitable and religious\n'
  'endowments and religious institutions.\n'
  '\n'
  '29\\. Prevention of the extension from one State to another of infectious '
  'or\n'
  'contagious diseases or pests affecting men, animals or plants.\n'
  '\n'
  '30\\. Vital statistics including registration of births and deaths.\n'
  '\n'
  '31\\. Ports other than those declared by or under law made by Parliament '
  'or\n'
  'existing law to be major ports.\n'
  '\n'
  '32\\. Shipping and navigation on inland waterways as regards mechanically\n'
  'propelled vessels, and the rule of the road on such waterways, and the '
  'carriage\n'
  'of passengers and goods on inland waterways subject to the provisions of '
  'List I\n'
  'with respect to national waterways.\n'
  '\n'
  '2[33. Trade and commerce in, and the production, supply and distribution\n'
  'of,\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the products of any industry where the control of such industry\n'
  'by the Union is declared by Parliament by law to be expedient in the\n'
  'public interest, and imported goods of the same kind as such products;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) foodstuffs, including edible oilseeds and oils;\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) cattle fodder, including oilcakes and other concentrates;\n'
  '(d) raw cotton, whether ginned or unginned, and cotton seed; and\n'
  '(e) raw jute.]\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Forty-second Amendment) Act, 1976, s. 57 '
  '(w.e.f. 3-1-1977).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Third Amendment) Act, 1954, s. 2 for entry '
  '33\n'
  '(w.e.f. 22-2-1955).\n'

  '41\\. Custody, management and disposal of property (including agricultural\n'

  '\n'
  '3[42. Acquisition and requisitioning of property.]\n'
  '\n'

  'respect to any of the matters in this List.\n'
  '\n'

  'fees\n'
  'taken in any court.\n'

  '# PART XX AMENDMENT OF THE CONSTITUTION\n'
  '\n'
  '368\\. "[Power of Parliament to amend the Constitution and\n'
  'procedure therefor] .- 2[(1) Notwithstanding anything in this '
  'Constitution,\n'
  'Parliament may in exercise of its constituent power amend by way of '
  'addition,\n'
  'variation or repeal any provision of this Constitution in accordance with '
  'the\n'
  'procedure laid down in this article.]\n'
  '\n'
  '3[(2)] An amendment of this Constitution may be initiated only by the\n'
  'introduction of a Bill for the purpose in either House of Parliament, and '
  'when\n'
  'the Bill is passed in each House by a majority of the total membership of '
  'that\n'
  'House and by a majority of not less than two-thirds of the members of that\n'
  'House present and voting, 4[it shall be presented to the President who '
  'shall give\n'
  'his assent to the Bill and thereupon] the Constitution shall stand amended '
  'in\n'
  'accordance with the terms of the Bill:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided that if such amendment seeks to make any change in-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) article 54, article 55, article 73, 5[ article 162, article 241 or\n'
  'article 279A]; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) Chapter IV of Part V, Chapter V of Part VI, or Chapter I of Part XI; '
  'or\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) any of the Lists in the Seventh Schedule; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(d) the representation of States in Parliament; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(e) the provisions of this article,\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Subs. by the Constitution (Twenty-fourth Amendment) Act, 1971, s. 3, '
  'for "Procedure\n'
  'for amendment of the Constitution" (w.e.f. 5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Ins. by s. 3, ibid. (w.e.f. 5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '3\\. Art. 368 re-numbered as cl. (2) thereof by s. 3, ibid. (w.e.f. '
  '5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '4\\. Subs. by s. 3, ibid., (w.e.f. 5-11-1971).\n'
  '\n'
  '5\\. Subs. by the Constitution (One Hundred and First Amendment) Act, 2016, '
  's. 15, for the\n'
  'words and figures "article 162 or article 241" (w.e.f. 16-9-2016).\n'
  '\n'

  'the amendment shall also require to be ratified by the Legislatures of not '
  'less\n'

  'Legislatures before the Bill making provision for such amendment is '

  '\n'

  'Part III) made or purporting to have been made under this article [whether '
  'before\n'
  'or after the commencement of section 55 of the Constitution (Forty-second\n'
  'Amendment) Act, 1976] shall be called in question in any court on any '
  'ground.\n'

  'no\n'
  'limitation whatever on the constituent power of Parliament to amend by way '
  'of\n',
  'substantially true report of any proceedings of either House of Parliament '
  'or the\n'

  'Legislature,\n'
  'of a State, unless the publication is proved to have been made with '

  'Legislature,\n'
  'of a State.\n'

  '(2) Clause (1) shall apply in relation to reports or matters broadcast by\n'

  'matters\n'

  'Explanation .- In this article, "newspaper" includes a news agency report\n'
  'containing material for publication in a newspaper.]\n'

  '2[361B. Disqualification for appointment on remunerative political\n'
  'post .- A member of a House belonging to any political party who is\n'
  'disqualified for being a member of the House under paragraph 2 of the '
  'Tenth\n'
  'Schedule shall also be disqualified to hold any remunerative political post '
  'for\n'
  'duration of the period commencing from the date of his disqualification '
  'till the\n'
  'date on which the term of his office as such member would expire or till '
  'the\n'
  'date on which he contests an election to a House and is declared elected,\n'
  'whichever is earlier.\n'
  '\n'
  'Explanation .- For the purposes of this article,-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the expression "House" has the meaning assigned to it in\n'
  'clause (a) of paragraph 1 of the Tenth Schedule;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) the expression "remunerative political post" means any office-\n'
  '\n'
  '(i) under the Government of India or the Government of a\n'
  'State where the salary or remuneration for such office is paid\n'
  'out of the public revenue of the Government of India or the\n'
  'Government of the State, as the case may be; or\n'

  '363\\. Bar to interference by courts in disputes arising out of certain\n'
  'treaties, agreements, etc .- (1) Notwithstanding anything in this '
  'Constitution\n'
  'but subject to the provisions of article 143, neither the Supreme Court nor '
  'any\n'
  'other court shall have jurisdiction in any dispute arising out of any '
  'provision of\n'
  'a treaty, agreement, covenant, engagement, sanad or other similar '
  'instrument\n'
  'which was entered into or executed before the commencement of this\n'
  'Constitution by any Ruler of an Indian State and to which the Government '
  'of\n'
  'the Dominion of India or any of its predecessor Governments was a party '
  'and\n'
  'which has or has been continued in operation after such commencement, or '
  'in\n'
  'any dispute in respect of any right accruing under or any liability or '
  'obligation\n'
  'arising out of any of the provisions of this Constitution relating to any '
  'such\n'
  'treaty, agreement, covenant, engagement, sanad or other similar '
  'instrument.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) In this article-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) "Indian State" means any territory recognised before the\n'
  'commencement of this Constitution by His Majesty or the Government\n'
  'of the Dominion of India as being such a State; and\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) "Ruler" includes the Prince, Chief or other person recognised\n'
  'before such commencement by His Majesty or the Government of the\n'
  'Dominion of India as the Ruler of any Indian State.\n'
  '\n'
  '1[363A. Recognition granted to Rulers of Indian States to cease and\n'
  'privy purses to be abolished .- Notwithstanding anything in this '
  'Constitution\n'
  'or in any law for the time being in force-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) the Prince, Chief or other person who, at any time before\n'
  'the commencement of the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment)\n'
  'Act, 1971, was recognised by the President as the Ruler of an Indian\n'
  'State or any person who, at any time before such commencement, was\n'
  'recognised by the President as the successor of such ruler shall, on and\n'
  'from such commencement, cease to be recognised as such Ruler or the\n'
  'successor of such Ruler;\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 363A ins. by the Constitution (Twenty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1971, '
  's. 3\n'
  '(w.e.f. 28-12-1971).\n'

  'accordingly the Ruler or, as the case may be, the successor of such\n'
  'Ruler, referred to in clause (a) or any other person shall not be paid any\n'

  '364\\. Special provisions as to major ports and aerodromes .- (1)\n'
  'Notwithstanding anything in this Constitution, the President may by public\n'
  'notification direct that as from such date as may be specified in the\n'
  'notification-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) any law made by Parliament or by the Legislature of a State\n'
  'shall not apply to any major port or aerodrome or shall apply thereto\n'
  'subject to such exceptions or modifications as may be specified in the\n'
  'notification; or\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) any existing law shall cease to have effect in any major port or\n'
  'aerodrome except as respects things done or omitted to be done before\n'
  'the said date, or shall in its application to such port or aerodrome have\n'
  'effect subject to such exceptions or modifications as may be specified in\n'
  'the notification.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) In this article-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) "major port" means a port declared to be a major port by or\n'
  'under any law made by Parliament or any existing law and includes all\n'
  'areas for the time being included within the limits of such port;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) "aerodrome" means aerodrome as defined for the purposes of\n'
  'the enactments relating to airways, aircraft and air navigation.\n'
  '\n'
  '365\\. Effect of failure to comply with, or to give effect to, directions\n'
  'given by the Union .- Where any State has failed to comply with, or to '
  'give\n'
  'effect to, any directions given in the exercise of the executive power of '
  'the Union\n'
  'under any of the provisions of this Constitution, it shall be lawful for '
  'the\n'
  'President to hold that a situation has arisen in which the Government of '
  'the State\n'
  'cannot be carried on in accordance with the provisions of this '
  'Constitution.\n'
  '\n'

  'assigned to them, that is to say-\n'
  '\n'

  'for the purposes of the enactments relating to Indian income-tax;\n'

  '\n'
  'Provided that if any question arises whether any matter is or is not a\n'
  'matter as respects which the Governor is under this clause required to act\n'
  'in the exercise of his individual judgment, the decision of the Governor '
  'in\n'
  'his discretion shall be final, and the validity of anything done by the\n'
  'Governor shall not be called in question on the ground that he ought or\n'
  'ought not to have acted in the exercise of his individual judgment:\n'
  '\n'
  'Provided further that if the President on receipt of a report from\n'
  'the Governor or otherwise is satisfied that it is no longer necessary for\n'
  'the Governor to have special responsibility with respect to law and order\n'
  'in the State of Arunachal Pradesh, he may by order direct that the\n'
  'Governor shall cease to have such responsibility with effect from such\n'

  'shall consist of not less than thirty members.]\n'

  '\n'
  '2[371J. Special provisions with respect to State of Karnataka .-\n'
  '(1) The President may, by order made with respect to the State of '
  'Karnataka,\n'
  'provide for any special responsibility of the Governor for-\n'
  '\n'
  '(a) establishment of a separate development board for Hyderabad-\n'
  'Karnataka region with the provision that a report on the working of the\n'
  'board will be placed each year before the State Legislative Assembly;\n'
  '\n'
  '(b) equitable allocation of funds for developmental expenditure\n'
  'over the said region, subject to the requirements of the State as a whole;\n'
  'and\n'
  '\n'
  '(c) equitable opportunities and facilities for the people belonging\n'
  'to the said region, in matters of public employment, education and\n'
  'vocational training, subject to the requirements of the State as a whole.\n'
  '\n'
  '(2) An order made under sub- clause (c) of clause (1) may provide for-\n'
  '(a) reservation of a proportion of seats educational and vocational\n'
  'training institutions in the Hyderabad-Karnataka region for students who\n'
  'belong to that region by birth or by domicile; and\n'
  '\n'
  '1\\. Art. 371-I ins. by the Constitution (Fifty-sixth Amendment) Act, 1987, '
  's. 2\n'
  '(w.e.f. 30-5-1987).\n'
  '\n'
  '2\\. Art. 371J ins. by the Constitution (Ninety-eighth Amendment) Act, '
  '2012, s. 2 (w.e.f.\n'
  '1-10-2013).\n'
  '\n'
